The azx_init_chip function, which is called during both initial probe and resume operations, does not reset the polling_mode and poll_count flags. When a codec timeout occurs before suspend, polling_mode is set to 1. After resume, azx_init_chip is called but fails to reset this flag, causing the driver to remain stuck in polling mode instead of using interrupt-based communication. This leads to the choppy audio symptoms reported. Additionally, the polling mode and poll_count can cause the driver to disable MSI and fall back to single_cmd mode. The fix requires resetting chip->polling_mode = 0 and chip->poll_count = 0 in the azx_init_chip function right after the hardware reset and before setting chip->initialized = 1, or alternatively in the azx_resume function before calling azx_init_chip.\"\n    11→}\n    12→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. The azx_init_chip function, which is called during both initial probe and resume operations, does not reset the polling_mode and poll_count flags. When a codec timeout occurs before suspend, polling_mode is set to 1. After resume, azx_init_chip is called but fails to reset this flag, causing the driver to remain stuck in polling mode instead of using interrupt-based communication. This leads to the choppy audio symptoms reported. Additionally, the polling mode and poll_count can cause the driver to disable MSI and fall back to single_cmd mode. The fix requires resetting chip->polling_mode = 0 and chip->poll_count = 0 in the azx_init_chip function right after the hardware reset and before setting chip->initialized = 1, or alternatively in the azx_resume function before calling azx_init_chip.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":6,"oldLines":6,"newStart":6,"newLines":6,"lines":["     \"azx_init_chip\",","     \"azx_resume\"","   ],","-  \"confidence\": 0.9,","+  \"confidence\": 0.95,","   \"reasoning\": \"The HDA Intel driver fails after suspend to RAM due to state not being properly reset. Now I see the complete picture. The error flow is:\n\n1. First timeout (line 898-905):\n   - If not in polling_mode and poll_count < 2\n   - Try polling once (do_poll = 1)\n   - Increment poll_count (becomes 1)\n   - Retry (goto again)\n\n2. Second timeout (line 908-914):\n   - If still not in polling_mode\n   - Switch to polling_mode = 1\n   - Retry (goto again)\n\n3. Third+ timeout with MSI enabled (line 916-929):\n   - If chip->msi is enabled\n   - Print \"No response from codec, disabling MSI\"\n   - Disable MSI\n   - Acquire IRQ again\n   - Retry (goto again)\n\n4. Final timeout (line 948-957):\n   - Print \"switching to single_cmd mode\"\n   - Set chip->single_cmd = 1\n   - Free command I/O\n\nThe issue is clear: if polling_mode or poll_count are not reset on resume, the codec communication will be stuck in polling mode or will quickly escalate through these error recovery modes.\n\nAfter resume, if there's any codec communication (e.g., from snd_hda_resume), and if polling_mode is still set to 1, then:\n- Every codec access will use polling mode (line 875)\n- This might cause issues with timing or synchronization\n- If another timeout occurs, it will skip the first two recovery steps and go straight to the MSI disabling or single_cmd fallback\n\nThis matches the user's symptoms:\n1. Sound works after boot (fresh state, polling_mode = 0)\n2. After suspend/resume, if a timeout occurred before suspend, polling_mode would be 1\n3. The system would be stuck in polling mode or would immediately escalate to MSI disabling\n4. This would cause choppy audio\n\nThe fix is definitely to reset polling_mode and poll_count in azx_init_chip.\n\n\npoll_count also needs resetting since it gates the first recovery attempt—if it's The azx_init_chip function, which is called during both initial probe and resume operations, does not reset the polling_mode and poll_count flags. When a codec timeout occurs before suspend, polling_mode is set to 1. After resume, azx_init_chip is called but fails to reset this flag, causing the driver to remain stuck in polling mode instead of using interrupt-based communication. This leads to the choppy audio symptoms reported. Additionally, the polling mode and poll_count can cause the driver to disable MSI and fall back to single_cmd mode. The fix requires resetting chip->polling_mode = 0 and chip->poll_count = 0 in the azx_init_chip function right after the hardware reset and before setting chip->initialized = 1, or alternatively in the azx_resume function before calling azx_init_chip.\"\n    11→}\n    12→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware.
